sacrifice for one's beliefs [Theo risked life and limb to ensure that Kee and her newborn made it safely to the "Human Project" safe haven in an effort to save the human race from extinction.]
lawless anarchy dystopia [The film is set in a near future where Britain is in the midst of descending into lawless anarchy.]
the horrors of war [The authoritarian British government was in a war against revolutionaries, and people suffered from it left and right.]
coping with the death of a friend [Theo was harrowed by the deaths and killings of people he knew, and by the death of Jasper in particular.]
coping with the death of a lover [Theo was harrowed by the sudden killing of the estranged wife, Julian, with whom he briefly got reacquainted.]
social activism [Much was made of Theo, Julian, and Jasper being former activists.]
facing organized pursuit [Theo and Kee were under hot pursuit by both British government forces and members of a militant immigrant-rights group.]
what it is like to be pregnant [The story follows the asylum seeker Kee's experience of being eight months pregnant while on the run from the authorities and a band of revolutionaries.]
refugee crisis [The story is set in a near future Britain that is being deluged by refugees fleeing from chaos in their own countries.]
what it is like to be a refugee [The story explores Kee's experience as an asylum seeker in a land that has taken a hard line against the mass influx of refugees into its territory.]

resistance movement [The Fishes militant immigrant-rights group was fighting a revolutionary war against the United Kingdom government.]

speculative technology [The Snow White surveillance system enabled the FBI to look up to four days into the past. The system worked by integrating data from several satellites to form a triangulated image of past events.]
murder [Central to the plot was Agent Carlin's getting to the bottom of the murder of Claire Kuchever.]

speed of light limitation [Dr. Denny explained that we are always looking into the past since "even light reflected from yourself in the mirror takes some time to reflect back."]
traversable wormhole [It turned out that the Snow White system had in fact generated a wormhole, which Agent Carlin subsequently passed through to find himself several days in the past.]
one cannot cheat fate [Agent Carlin wasn't buying it when Dr. Denny told him that it was physically impossible to change the past. Dr. Denny used both of the words "fate" and "destiny" in his explanation.]

:: Title
The Man from Earth

:: Date

:: Description
The Man from Earth is a 2007 American drama science fiction film written by
Jerome Bixby and directed by Richard Schenkman. It stars David Lee Smith as
John Oldman, the protagonist. The screenplay was conceived by Jerome Bixby in
the early 1960s and completed on his deathbed in April 1998.

Synopsis: A departing university professor claims to be a prehistoric caveman
who has secretly survived for more than 14,000 years.

District 9 is a 2009 science fiction action horror film directed by Neill
Blomkamp, written by Blomkamp and Terri Tatchell, and produced by Peter
Jackson and Carolynne Cunningham. It is a co-production of New Zealand, the
United States, and South Africa. The film stars Sharlto Copley, Jason Cope,
and David James, and was adapted from Blomkamp's 2006 short film Alive in
Joburg.

:: Major Themes
refugee crisis [a space ship of alien refugees came to Johannesburg]
threat from extraterrestrial life [a space ship of alien refugees came to Johannesburg]
social oppression [Aliens were made to live in slum under harsh conditions.]
forced resettlement [aliens forced to move from their current slum to a new one]
racial segregation [The aliens lived segregated from human in a sprawling slum.]
xenophobia in society [The humans were racist against the insectoids refugees and segregated them in a big slum.]
human rights issue [aliens treated inhumanely even though protections were initially granted protections]
what if I underwent a physical metamorphosis [Wikus metamorphosed into an insectoid]
human-bug hybrid [Wikus metamorphosed into an insectoid looking creature.]
unethical business practices [The MNU corporation secured a government contract to relocate alien refugees, but they violated the aliens "human" rights and were moreover fixated on acquiring the alien's advanced weaponry.]
human self-sacrifice [Wikus risks his life fighting paramilitary force in orer to save Christopher and his son]
from zero to hero [Wikus went from being an incompetent paper pusher to being a hero.]
sentient rights [aliens not given full human rights even thought they were sentient and intelligent]

:: Minor Themes
insectoid being [a space ship of insectoid refugees came to Johannesburg]
nepotism [Wikus promoted to lead operation to move aliens to new area because he was married to daughter of man who ran company responsible for the operation]
husband and wife [Wikus and his wife]
father and daughter [corporation CEO and his daughter]
father and son [Christopher and his insectoid son]
powered exoskeleton [Wikus in alien robotic exoskeleton]


movie: Universal Soldier: Regeneration (2009)
=============================================

:: Title
Universal Soldier: Regeneration

:: Date
2009-10-01

:: Description
It is up to the former UniSol Luc Devereaux to stop a group of terrorists from
killing the Ukrainian Prime Minister's children, whom they have taken hostage,
and also from blowing up the Chernobyl Nuclear Power Plant. It is the fifth
installment in the Universal Soldier film series.

:: References
https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Soldier:_Regeneration

:: Ratings
2 <paul>

:: Choice Themes
supersoldier [Central to the film is a rogue military program to harvest dead soldiers, re-animate and genetically enhanced them with the objective of creating an army of remorseless killers.]

:: Major Themes
ransom kidnapping [A group of terrorists kidnapped the Ukrainian Prime Minister's son and daughter and held them hostage, demanding the release of their imprisoned comrades within 72 hours.]
revival long after death [Fundamental to the film is a technology to recycle battlefield dead into remorseless supersoldiers.]
facing a hostage situation [Luc was sent in to rescue Ukrainian Prime Minister's son and daughter who were being held as hostages by terrorists.]
reintegrating into society [The former UniSol Luc was undergoing rehabilitation therapy with the goal of rejoining society before he was commandeered by the military to go on a dangerous mission.]

:: Minor Themes
nuclear power safety [The Chernobyl nuclear accident was described.]
speculative genetic engineering [It was mentioned that the next generation Universal Soldiers had been improved through unspecified genetic modifications.]
doctor and patient [Dr. Sandra Fleming was helping Luc reintegrate into society.]
military related work [Captain Kevin Burke and other army grunts battled terrorists.]


movie: Avatar (2009)
====================

:: Title
Avatar

:: Date
2009-12-10

:: Description
Avatar (marketed as James Cameron's Avatar) is a 2009 American epic science
fiction film directed, written, produced, and co-edited by James Cameron and
starring Sam Worthington, Zoe Saldana, Stephen Lang, Michelle Rodriguez, and
Sigourney Weaver.

Synopsis: Set in the mid-22nd century, humans are colonizing Pandora, a lush
habitable moon of a gas giant in the Alpha Centauri star system, in order to
mine the valuable mineral unobtanium. The expansion of the mining colony
threatens the continued existence of a local tribe of Na'vi – a humanoid
species indigenous to Pandora.

:: References
https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avatar_(2009_film)

:: Ratings
2 <paul>

:: Major Themes
space colonization [Central to the story was that humans had set up a mining colony on a moon in the Alpha Centauri star system and were going about displacing its native inhabitants.]
habitable moon [A main novelty of the film is that it is set on a lush habitable moon, named Pandora, of a gas giant in the Alpha Centauri star system.]
military related work [The viewer is shown what it might be like for ordinary soldiers to have to fight in unfamiliar terrain for a dubious cause. The wheelchair-bound former Marine Jake was a self-described jarhead.]
coping with a disability [Much was made of the wheelchair-bound former Marine Jake savoring the experience of remotely controlling a fully functional Na'vi alien body with his brain.]
extraterrestrial being [Pandora was inhabited by the Na'vi, a species of 10-foot tall, blue-skinned, sentient humanoids.]
attack from outer space by a powerful conquering enemy [From the Na'vi point of view, the humans came down down from the sky to overrun the land they'd inhabited for untold generations.]
colonialism [The RDA mining corporation was going about subjugating the Na'vi based on stereotypical European colonial period practices. In particular, the corporation officials were quick to resort to brute force to get what they wanted when offers of schools and roads failed to win over the Na'vi.]
speculative technology [A main novelty of the film is a special technology enabling people to remotely operate special Na'vi alien bodies.]
noble savage utopia [The Na'vi lived in harmony with nature and worshiped a mother goddess named Eywa.]
romantic love [One storyline followed Jake and the Na'vi princess Neytiri as they fell passionately in love.]
attachment to one's land [Central to the story was that the Na'vi were not going to let the human colonists push them off their sacred land.]
organized religion [The religious practices of the Na'vi were much explored. They worshiped a mother goddess name Eywa, practiced a form of ancestor veneration, held all live sacred, etc.]
unethical business practices [The RDA mining corporation having no qualms about wiping out the Na'vi aliens in order to mine the valuable element unobtanium was at the heart of the story.]

:: Minor Themes
depletion of a vital natural resource [It was explained that by 2154, humans had depleted Earth's natural resources with a severe energy crisis being the result.]
cryogenic technology [Jake and others were revived from cryogenic stasis upon arriving at the habitable moon Pandora.]
coping with the death of a family member [Jake solemnly observed his recently deceased bother Tommy being cremated. People spoke in glowing terms of Jake's deceased brother Tommy.]
interstellar space travel [The crew had traveled approximately 6 light years to reach a habitable moon in the Alpha Centauri star system.]
speculative spaceship [The crew traveled to the habitable moon Pandora in the futuristic, interstellar voyage capable starship the ISV Venture Star.]
powered exoskeleton [The soldiers were stomping around in robotic armored units complete with powerful arms and legs.]
hologram [Holographic maps of different regions of Pandora were on display in the command center.]
human vs. beast [Jake had to stand his ground upon encountering a large territorial beast that charged at him. Jake came face to face with a variety of other dangerous beasts in the forests of Pandora.]
father and daughter [Neytiri's father was the leader of her clan.]
mother and daughter [Neytiri's mother was the shaman of their clan.]
pleasure in nature [Jake and the others were in awe of the floating mountains of Pandora.]
hunting [Jake hunted a deer-like animal in the traditional Na'vi fashion.]
rite of passage into manhood [Jake completed a series of trials that qualified him as a man of the Omaticaya clan.]
betrayal [Neytiri pointedly accused Jake of having betrayed her clan for not having revealed that he'd originally been sent to infiltrate them.]
coping with the death of a parent [Neytiri released a scream of mourning upon seeing the body of her slaughtered father.]
shamanism [Mo'at performed a shamanistic ritual over Jake's body.]
coping with the death of someone [Jake mourned the deaths of his comrades in arms Trudy and Grace.]
